Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses two related topics: vinegar derived from wine, and wine dregs. The author begins by stating the Hanafi ruling that vinegar from wine is pure and permissible regardless of whether it becomes vinegar spontaneously or through human intervention (e.g., adding salt, moving to sun). This is in contrast to Imam al-Shafi'i, who holds that vinegar made by adding something is not permissible. The Hanafi proof is the hadith 'Naim illa dam al-khal' (Yes, except blood and vinegar) which is general, and also a qiyas (analogy) with slaughtering: just as slaughtering transforms an animal from impure to pure, making vinegar transforms wine from impure to pure. The text also mentions a minority view that it does not become pure because of the disrespect shown to wine, but the correct view is that it does. For the method of transformation, if the container was purified by the vinegar, it becomes pure. The text then discusses cases like adding wine to soup—it remains impure and the drinker is not flogged because he drank impure liquid, not wine. Kneading dough with wine makes the dough impure. Next, the author turns to wine dregs (the sediment). Drinking dregs is makruh (disliked) because it contains parts of wine, and using it for any purpose is haram. However, the hadd punishment for drinking dregs is only applied if the drinker becomes intoxicated, contrary to al-Shafi'i who would apply hadd for any amount. The Hanafi reasoning is that hadd is for deterrent on substances the soul desires; since dregs are not desired, the penalty is lighter. The text ends by mentioning the dislike of using wine for enema or urethral instillation.

Key Terms
دردي الخمر (durdiyy al-khamr): The sediment or dregs left at the bottom of wine.
الاحتقان (al-ihtiqan): The use of an enema, here with wine.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what condition does the Hanafi school impose the hadd punishment for drinking wine dregs?
A) If the person drinks any amount.
B) If the person becomes intoxicated.
C) If the person knew it was dregs.
D) Never, because dregs are not wine.

Key Takeaway
Wine dregs are impure and prohibited for any use, but the hadd punishment for drinking them only applies if intoxication occurs, based on the Hanafi understanding that hadd is for deterrent on substances the soul desires.

The Hanafi Rule for Permissibility of Boiled Grape Juice
Detailed ruling on the two-thirds evaporation rule for grape juice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that boiled grape juice is permissible only when two-thirds have evaporated, and apply the calculation method to determine when the remaining liquid is halal.

Core Idea
Grape juice becomes halal only when two-thirds of it have evaporated by boiling — foam and poured liquid do not count.

In Hanafi fiqh, the permissibility of drinking grape juice that has been boiled depends on a precise quantitative measure: two-thirds of the liquid must evaporate. This principle prevents the consumption of any intoxicating residue. The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq elaborates on this rule, including how to handle added water, prematurely poured liquid, and cases involving dates or sun-drying. By studying this lesson, you will master the fundamental ruling and its practical applications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Principle
Understand that the baseline ruling is: boiled grape juice becomes halal when two-thirds of its volume have evaporated by boiling, leaving one-third. The foam (zabad) that rises is not counted as part of the two-thirds.
This is the central rule from which all subcases derive.
2
Handle Added Water
If water is added before boiling, determine whether the water evaporates faster or at the same rate as the juice. If faster, wait until two-thirds of the total mixture (including water) have evaporated. If at the same rate, boil until all that remains is one-third of the original juice plus water.
The added water is considered part of the mixture for measurement.
3
Apply the Calculation for Partial Evaporation and Pouring
If less than one-third evaporates and then some liquid is poured out, the remaining is not permissible until two-thirds of the original amount have been removed by boiling. Use the given formula: take one-third of the total, multiply by what remains after pouring, divide by what remained after boiling before pouring. The result is the permissible amount that must remain after further boiling.
The example with 12 ratls illustrates the method.
4
Review Special Cases
Note the rulings from Abu Yusuf (dates added to cooked juice) and Abu Hanifa (sun-drying equivalent to boiling; mixing with mustard). Also understand that if juice becomes intoxicating before completing the two-thirds evaporation, further cooking does not make it permissible.
These cases expand the principle to similar scenarios.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في طبخ العصير : الأصل فيه أن ما ذهب بغليانه بالنار وقذفه بالزبد لا يعتقد به حتى يذهب ثلثاه فيجل الثلث الباقي بعده ولو صب فيه الماء قبل الطبخ ثم طبخ بماء ينظر ؛ إن كان الماء أسرع ذهاباً للطافته ولرقته يعتبر ذهاب ثلثيه بعد الماء الذي صب فيه كله وبعد ذهاب الزبد فيحل الثلث الباقي من العصير وإن كانا يذهبان معاً فيطبخ حتى يذهب الجميع بعد ذهاب الزبد فيحل ثلث الباقي لذهاب الثلثين وبقاء الثلث ماء وعصيراً. ولو طبخ العصير فذهب أقل من الثلث ثم أهرق الثلثين وبقي الثلث ماء وعصيراً ولو طبخ العصير فذهب أقل من الثلث ثم أهرق بعضه لا يحل الباقي حتى يذهب ثلثاه بالطبخ وطريق معرفته أن يؤخذ ثلث الجميع فيضرب به في الباقي ثم يقسم الخارج على ما بقي بعد ذهاب ما نقص منه بالطبخ قبل أن ينصب منه شيء، فما أصاب الواحد بالقسمة فذاك القدر هو الحلال ويطبخ الباقي إلى أن يبقى قدره فيحل مثاله : اثنا عشر رطلاً من العصير طبخ حتى ذهب أربعة أرطال ثم أهرق رطلين يؤخذ ثلث العصير كله وهو أربعة فيضرب فيما بقي بعد الأنصاب وهو ستة فيصير أربعة وعشرين فيقسمه على ما بقي بعد ذهاب ما ذهب منه بالطبخ قبل أن يهراق منه وذلك ثمانية فيصيب كل واحد منهم ثلاثة فيكون ذلك القدر هو الحلال فيطبخ الباقي إلى أن يبقى قدره فيحل . وإن شئت قسمت ما ذهب بالطبخ على المنصب وعلى ما بقي بعد الأنصباب فما أصاب المنصب يجعل مع المنصب كأنه لم يكن وكان جميع الباقي، وما أصابه من الذاهب بالطبخ فقد ذهب منه ذلك القدر فيطبخ حتى يذهب إلى تمام الثلثين. وإن شئت قلت إن الباقي بعد الطبخ قبل الأنصباب بعضه حلال وهو قدر ثلث المجموع، فإذا أهريق بعضه أهريق من الحلال بحسابه فيطبخ الباقي حتى يبقى قدر ما فيه من الحلال. وفي المحيط عن أبي يوسف طبخ ثم ألقى فيه تمراً فغلى قال : ما ألقى فيه لو نبذه على حدة كان منه نبيذاً فلا خير فيه لأن هذا مطبوخ ويعتبر، وإن كان يسيراً لا ينتبذ منه لا أفسده . يعتد به لأنه لا يحد فيه الشارب لانفراده، ولو صب قدح في خابية مطبوخ الإمام: إذا وضع في الشمس حتى ذهب ثلثاه وبقي ثلثه فلا بأس به فهو بمنزلة طبخه بالنار، وكذا إذا ملأ الخابية بالخردل وخلط فيها العصير ومضى على ذلك مدة ولم يشتد ولم يسكر فلا بأس به في قول أصحابنا . ولو طبخ عصيراً حتى ذهب ثلثه وتكره حتى يرد ثم أعاد الطبخ حتى ذهب نصف ما بقي فإذا أعاد الطبخ قبل أن يغلي وتغير عن حالة العصير فلا بأس به لأن الطبخ وجد قبل ثبوت الحرمة بالغليان والشدة، وإن عاد بعد أن غلى وتغير فلا خير فيه لأن طبخه وجد بعد ثبوت الحرمة فلا ينتفع به
Section on cooking grape juice: The principle is that what is removed by boiling over fire and throwing off foam is not counted until two-thirds are gone, so the remaining third is permissible. If water is poured into it before cooking and then cooked with water, it is considered: if the water goes away faster due to its lightness and thinness, then two-thirds are considered after the water that was poured into it entirely and after the foam goes away, so the remaining third of the juice is permissible. If they both go away together, then cook until all goes away after the foam, then the remaining third is permissible because two-thirds are gone and one-third remains as water and juice. If the juice is cooked and less than one-third goes away, then he pours out two-thirds, and one-third remains as water and juice. If the juice is cooked and less than one-third goes away, then he pours some of it, the remainder is not permissible until two-thirds go away by cooking. The method of knowing it: take one-third of the total, multiply it by the remainder, then divide the product by what remains after the decrease from cooking before anything is poured out. Whatever each unit gets by division, that amount is permissible, and cook the remainder until it remains that amount, then it becomes permissible. Example: twelve ratls of juice cooked until four ratls went away, then he poured two ratls. Take one-third of all the juice, which is four, multiply by what remains after the pouring, which is six, becomes twenty-four, divide it by what remains after what went away by cooking before pouring, which is eight, so each of them gets three. That amount is permissible, so cook the remainder until it remains that amount, then it becomes permissible. If you wish, divide what went away by cooking between the poured amount and what remains after pouring. What corresponds to the poured amount is considered with the poured amount as if it had not been, and all that remains is the remainder. And what corresponds to what went away by cooking has gone from it that amount, so cook until it goes away to complete two-thirds. If you wish, you may say: the remainder after cooking before pouring is partly permissible, which is an amount equal to one-third of the total. So if some of it is poured, the permissible part is poured proportionally, so cook the remainder until only the amount of the permissible part remains. In al-Muhit from Abu Yusuf: He cooked then threw in dates and it boiled. He said: 'If what he threw in were left separately, it would become date-wine, so there is no good in it because this is cooked and considered.' And if it is a small amount from which date-wine is not made, it does not spoil it. It is counted because the drinker is not punished for it being separate. If a cup is poured into a cask of cooked juice (Imam Abu Hanifa said): If it is placed in the sun until two-thirds go and one-third remains, there is no harm, it is like cooking it with fire. Similarly, if he fills the cask with mustard and mixes juice in it, and time passes without it becoming strong or intoxicating, there is no harm according to our companions. If he cooks juice until one-third goes and it becomes thick, then returns and repeats cooking until half of what remains goes, then if he repeats cooking before it boils and changes from the state of juice, there is no harm because cooking occurred before prohibition by boiling and strength. If he repeats after it boiled and changed, there is no good in it because cooking occurred after prohibition, so it is not benefited from.
Source pages p. 405

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq provides the detailed fiqh rules for when boiled grape juice ( عصير ) becomes permissible to drink. The passage type is a ruling statement with practical examples. The principle is: when grape juice is boiled, it becomes halal (permissible) only after two-thirds of it have evaporated, leaving one-third. The foam that rises is not counted as part of the two-thirds. If water is added before boiling, the ruling depends on whether the water evaporates faster or together with the juice. If water evaporates faster, you must wait until two-thirds of the total mixture (including water) have evaporated. If they evaporate together, boil until all that remains is one-third of the original juice plus water. If less than one-third evaporates and then some of the juice is poured out, it is not permissible until two-thirds of the remaining liquid have evaporated by boiling. The author provides a calculation method for determining how much must be boiled further. He also relates a narration from Abu Yusuf: if someone adds dates to cooked juice and it boils, it is not permissible if the dates alone would have produced date-wine, but if the amount is small so that it would not produce intoxicating date-wine, it does not spoil it. Imam Abu Hanifa states that sun-drying is equivalent to boiling: if two-thirds evaporate in the sun, the juice becomes permissible. Similarly, mixing juice with mustard in a cask and letting it sit without becoming intoxicating is permissible. Finally, if juice is cooked partially and becomes thick, and then the cooking is repeated, it is permissible if the second cooking occurs before the juice has boiled and become intoxicating; if it has already become intoxicating, the second cooking does not make it permissible.

Key Terms
العصير (al-ʿasīr): The juice of grapes (or other fruits) before it becomes wine.
الطبخ (al-ṭabkh): Boiling or cooking the juice over fire to remove alcohol.
الزبد (al-zabad): The foam that rises to the top when juice is boiled; it is not counted toward the two-thirds that must evaporate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If you boil grape juice and one-third evaporates, then you pour out half of the remaining liquid, what must you do?
A) It is already halal because you removed some liquid.
B) Boil the remaining until two-thirds of the original total have evaporated by boiling.
C) Boil the remaining until two-thirds of the poured-out amount have evaporated.
D) It is never halal once poured after partial boiling.

Key Takeaway
Boiled grape juice becomes halal only when two-thirds of its volume have evaporated by boiling, and any manual removal of liquid does not substitute for evaporation.

Ruling on Pawning with Unspecified Loan Amount
Expansion on pawn destruction before loan disbursement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mortgagee liability when a pawn is destroyed before the loan is disbursed, both when the loan amount is specified and unspecified, and identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding the minimum compensation.

Core Idea
If a pawn is destroyed before the loan, the mortgagee must pay the specified amount or, if unspecified, whatever he wishes.

This lesson examines a specific ruling in the law of pawn (rahn) from the commentary Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. The scenario involves a pawn destroyed before the mortgagee gives the loan. The key question is whether the mortgagee is liable and what amount he must pay. The passage also reveals an intra-Hanafi difference concerning the minimum acceptable compensation based on custom.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Understand the two variants: (1) pawn with a specifically promised loan amount, (2) pawn with an unspecified loan amount. Note that in both cases the pawn is destroyed before the loan is given.
The pawn is a silver heart (qalb fiddah) used as an example.
2
Understand the legal basis (qiyas)
The ruling is based on analogy: the pawn received on the condition of a loan is treated like a pawn received under a valid pawn contract, which itself is treated like an item received for price negotiation (all are guaranteed). Thus, the mortgagee is liable.
The chain: condition-based pawn → true pawn → purchase negotiation item.
3
Apply to specified loan
If the loan amount is specified (e.g., a dirham), the mortgagee must give that exact amount upon destruction of the pawn.
4
Apply to unspecified loan
If the loan amount is not specified, the mortgagee may give whatever he wishes because the vagueness came from the debtor. This is the position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Muhammad disapproves of giving less than a dirham because custom does not involve borrowing such small amounts. This is a legitimate difference based on 'urf.
The relied-upon position is that any amount is permitted, but less than a dirham is makruh tanzihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مذكور فيه وقوله مضمون . قال في العناية : قيل ذكر مضمون للتأكيد، وقيل احترازاً عن دين يجب كالرهن بالدرك وهو ضمان الدرك عند استحقاق المبيع. ولم يتعرض المؤلف لمسألة القلب قال في المبسوط : رهن قلب فضة على أن يقرضه درهماً فهلك قبل أن يقرضه يعطيه درهماً لأنه مقبوض على جهة الرهن والمقبوض بجهة الرهن كالمقبوض على حقيقة الرهن كالمقبوض على سوم الشراء. قال على أن أقرضه شيئاً ولم يسم شيئاً فهلك يعطيه ما شاء لأنه بالهلاك صار مستوفياً شيئاً فصار كأنه عند الهلاك. قال وجب لفلان علي شيء ولو قال امسكه رهناً بنفقة تعطيها إياه لأنه مستوفياً مالاً مجهولاً بالهلاك، ولو قال أمسكه رهناً بدراهم يلزمه ثلاثة يصير لأن أقل الجمع ثلاثة كما لو قال لفلان علي دراهم. وفي المنتقى : ولو رهنه رهناً على أن يقرضه ولم يسم القرض قال يعطيه المرتهن ما شاء، فإن قال أعطيك فلساً قال محمد رحمه الله تعالى : لا أستحسن أقل من درهم لأنه مقبوض على سوم الرهن ولا تسمية في القرض فلا يمكن اعتبار قيمته إذ لا تقدير في القرض فيعطيه ما شاء لأن الإبهام جاء من قبله ولا يصدق في أقل من لأن العادة لم تجر في اقتراض أقل من درهم، وهذه المسألة المذكورة في عيون مسائل لأبي درهم الليث أيضاً .
Mentioned in it and His saying: 'guaranteed.' Said in al-Inayah: It was said that 'guaranteed' was mentioned for emphasis, and it was said as a precaution against a debt that is obligatory, like pawning for the security against defect (al-darak), which is the guarantee of defect when the sold item is repossessed. And the author did not address the issue of the heart. He said in al-Mabsut: He pawned a silver heart with the condition that he lends him a dirham, and it was destroyed before he lent him, he gives him a dirham because it is received on the basis of pawn, and what is received on the basis of pawn is like what is received on the true basis of pawn, like what is received on the basis of purchase negotiation. He said: 'With the condition that I lend him something' and he did not specify something, and it was destroyed, he gives him whatever he wishes because by destruction it became as if he had taken possession of something, so it is as if at the time of destruction [he received it]. He said: 'An obligation is due to so-and-so' and if he said 'Hold it as a pawn for expenses you give him' because he received unknown property by destruction, and if he said 'Hold it as a pawn for dirhams' he owes three because the minimum of a plural is three, just as if he said 'To so-and-so I owe dirhams.' And in al-Muntaqa: If he pawns it with the condition that he lends him and did not name the loan, he said the mortgagee gives him whatever he wishes. If he says 'I give you a fals,' Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) said: I do not consider it good practice to give less than a dirham because it is received on the basis of pawn negotiation and there is no specification in the loan, so its value cannot be considered since there is no estimation in the loan, so he gives him whatever he wishes because the vagueness came from him, and he is not believed in (claiming) less than a dirham because custom does not involve borrowing less than a dirham. And this issue is mentioned in Uyun Masa'il of Abu Dirham al-Layth as well.
Source pages p. 435

Commentary
This passage is an expansion from the commentary Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on the matn Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It begins by explaining why the matn used the word 'مضمون' (guaranteed) in the context of pawn (رهن). The commentator mentions two reasons: first, for emphasis; second, to exclude cases where the debt is obligatory from the start, like pawning for the guarantee against defect (ضمان الدرك) in a sale. The author of Kanz did not address the specific issue of pawning a 'heart' (قلب), meaning a piece of silver in the shape of a heart, so the commentator brings it from Al-Mabsut. The ruling: If someone pawns a silver heart with the condition that the mortgagee lends him a dirham, and the pawn is destroyed before the loan is given, the mortgagee must give a dirham (i.e., the promised loan) because the pawn was received in a valid manner akin to a true pawn. If no specific loan amount is named, the mortgagee gives whatever he wishes, because by the destruction he is deemed to have received something (the pawn's value) and thus must compensate. If the debtor says 'Hold it as a pawn for expenses,' the mortgagee owes the expenses. If he says 'for dirhams,' he owes at least three dirhams because the plural implies a minimum of three. Al-Muntaqa adds that if the loan is unspecified, the mortgagee gives any amount. Imam Muhammad, however, disapproves of giving less than a dirham because custom does not support borrowing such a small amount. This is an intra-Hanafi difference where Muhammad gives a preference based on custom ('urf). The passage ends by noting this issue is also found in Uyun al-Masa'il of Abu Dirham al-Layth.

Key Terms
رهن (rahn): A pawn or pledge given as security for a debt; the mortgagee holds it as a trust until the debt is paid.
قلب فضة (qalb fiddah): A piece of silver shaped like a heart, used as a pawn in the example.
مضمون (madmun): Guaranteed; here it describes the pawn as being subject to liability if lost under certain conditions.
سوم الشراء (sawm al-shira): Price negotiation for purchase; an item taken for inspection during negotiation is guaranteed if destroyed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Al-Mabsut, if a pawn is destroyed and the loan amount was specified, what must the mortgagee do?
A) Pay nothing because the pawn was not legally held
B) Pay a dirham because the pawn was received on the basis of pawn
C) Pay the value of the pawn only
D) Pay whatever he wishes, but no less than three dirhams

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, if a pawn is destroyed before the loan is given, the mortgagee must compensate with the promised loan or, if unspecified, with any amount, though giving less than a dirham is disliked due to custom.

Abu Yusuf on Pawn: Liability and Binding Conditions
Abu Yusuf's rulings on pawn liability and conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a pawn is lost before the loan is given, apply the principle of 'madmun bi-aqalli min qimatihi wa min al-dayn', and explain why the loan condition binds the mortgagee but not the pawner.

Core Idea
The pawn is guaranteed by the lesser of its value and the debt; loan conditions bind the mortgagee but not the pawner.

This lesson explores two rulings transmitted from Abu Yusuf on the liability of a mortgagee when a pawn is lost before the loan is given. The first case involves an unspecified loan amount, the second a specified loan, and the third a complex case of pawning two animals. These rulings illustrate the Hanafi principle that the pawn is guaranteed by the lesser of its value and the debt, and the asymmetry in binding conditions between pawner and mortgagee.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of pawn case
Read the first scenario: the pawner says 'Lend me and take this pawn' without naming the loan amount. The pawn is lost before any loan is given. What is the ruling? Then identify the second scenario with a named loan (garment held for twenty dirhams). Finally, the two-animal case with a loan condition.
2
Apply the guarantee principle
For each case, determine the liability: the mortgagee pays the value of the pawn or the loan amount, whichever is less. This is the rule 'madmun bi-aqalli min qimatihi wa min al-dayn'.
The rule is applied whether the pawn is lost before or after the loan, but here it is before.
3
Analyze the option in the two-animal case
In the two-animal case, the mortgagee has an option: pay the value of the destroyed animal (50) or take the other animal and lend the 100. Understand why he is not compelled to lend, based on the binding nature of the pawn contract.
The pawn is binding on the pawner (he cannot take back the pawn), but conditions on the mortgagee (to lend) are binding on him if he takes the pawn.
4
Resolve disputes over value
Study the fiqh rule for when the pawner and mortgagee dispute the value of the lost pawn: the mortgagee's word is taken if he denies a higher claim, unless the other animal remains to determine value.
This is a standard rule: the statement of the denying party is given weight.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذكر المعلى عن أبي يوسف رحمهما الله تعالى : لو قال رجل اقرضني وخذ هذا الرهن ولم يسم القرض فأخذ الرهن فضاع ولم يقرضه قال عليه قيمة الرهن. ولو رهن ثوباً فقال أمسكه بعشرين درهماً فهلك الثوب عند المرتهن قبل أن يعطيه شيئاً فعليه قيمة الثوب إلا أن تجاوز قيمته عشرين لأن الرهن مضمون بأقل من قيمته ومن الدين. رهن دابتين على أن يقرضه مائة وقيمة أحدهما خمسون والأخرى ثلاثون فقبض وقبض التي قيمتها خمسون فهلكت برد خمسين لأنه مضمون بالقيمة لا بالمسمى كالمقبوض بجهة البيع فإن بداله أن يأخذ الأخرى ويقرضه له ذلك ولا يجبر على القرض لأن الرهن لازم من في جانب الراهن، فما شرط على الراهن في الرهن يكون لازماً وفي حق المرتهن غير لازم فما شرطه على المرتهن لا يكون لازماً والقرض مشروط على المرتهن فيكون لازماً في حقه. ولو هلكت إحداهما عند الراهن واختلفا في قيمة التي هلكت عند المرتهن فالقول للمرتهن لأن الراهن يدعي على المرتهن زيادة ضمان وهو ينكر، فإن بقيت إحداهما ينظر إلى قيمة الباقي فتظهر قيمة الهالك فلا يلتفت إلى اختلافهما لأنه أمكن معرفة ما وقع التنازع فيه لا من جهتهما
And al-Mualla mentioned from Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on them both): If a man says 'Lend me and take this pawn' and did not name the loan, and he took the pawn and it was lost and he did not lend him, he said: he is liable for the value of the pawn. And if he pawned a garment and said 'Hold it for twenty dirhams' and the garment was destroyed with the mortgagee before he gave him anything, he is liable for the value of the garment unless its value exceeds twenty, because the pawn is guaranteed by the lesser of its value and the debt. He pawned two animals with the condition that he lends him one hundred, and the value of one is fifty and the other thirty, and he took possession and took possession of the one worth fifty, and it was destroyed: he pays fifty because it is guaranteed by value, not by the named amount, like what is received on the basis of sale. However, it is up to him to take the other and lend him that, and he is not compelled to lend because the pawn is binding on the part of the pawner, so what is stipulated on the pawner in the pawn is binding, but on the part of the mortgagee it is not binding, so what is stipulated on the mortgagee is not binding, and the loan is stipulated on the mortgagee, so it is binding on his part. And if one of them is destroyed with the pawner and they dispute the value of the one destroyed with the mortgagee, the statement is of the mortgagee because the pawner claims an additional liability against the mortgagee and he denies. If one of them remains, the value of the remaining is considered and the value of the destroyed [animal] appears, so their dispute is not considered because it is possible to know what the dispute is about from other than them.
Source pages p. 435

Commentary
This passage contains two separate rulings transmitted from Abu Yusuf and a detailed case on pawning two animals. First, Abu Yusuf rules that if someone says 'Lend me and take this pawn' without specifying the loan amount, and the pawn is lost before the loan is given, the mortgagee must pay the value of the pawn (not the unspecified loan). This is a stricter view than the general Hanafi position which allows the mortgagee to pay what he wishes. Second, if a garment is pawned for a specific loan of twenty dirhams and is destroyed before the loan is given, the mortgagee pays the value of the garment but only up to twenty dirhams; if the garment is worth more, he pays only the loan amount. This is because the pawn is guaranteed by the lesser of its value and the debt. The third case: a man pawns two animals as security for a loan of one hundred dirhams, one animal worth fifty, the other thirty. The mortgagee takes possession of the fifty-dirham animal and it is destroyed. He must pay fifty because the pawn is guaranteed by its value, not by the named loan amount, analogous to an item received on a sale basis. However, the mortgagee has the option to instead take the other animal and lend the loan amount; he cannot be forced to lend. This is because the pawn contract is binding on the pawner (he must keep the pawn) but not on the mortgagee regarding the condition to lend; the loan is a condition on the mortgagee, so it is binding on him (he must lend if he takes the pawn). But if the other animal is lost with the pawner and they dispute the value of the one destroyed with the mortgagee, the mortgagee's word is taken because the pawner claims an extra liability which the mortgagee denies. If one animal remains, its value helps determine the destroyed animal's value, ending the dispute.

Key Terms
مضمون بأقل من قيمته ومن الدين (madmun bi-aqalli min qimatihi wa min al-dayn): The pawn is guaranteed by the lesser of its value and the debt amount; i.e., the mortgagee's liability is capped at the smaller of the two.
لازم (lazim): Binding; refers to a contractual obligation that cannot be unilaterally revoked.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of pawning two animals for a loan of 100 dirhams, if the mortgagee takes possession of the animal worth 50 dirhams and it is destroyed, what must he pay?
A) 100 dirhams because that was the loan amount
B) 50 dirhams, the value of the destroyed animal
C) Nothing, because the loan was never given
D) The value of both animals, i.e., 80 dirhams

Key Takeaway
Abu Yusuf's rulings establish that a pawn is guaranteed by the lesser of its value and the debt, and that loan conditions in pawn contracts bind the mortgagee but not the pawner in terms of forcing performance.

The Prohibition of Conditional Sale in Pawn
Prohibition of conditional sale in pawn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a pawn conditioned to become a sale upon default and explain the evidence from the hadith.

Core Idea
A pawn cannot automatically become a sale upon default; such a condition is void.

In this lesson, we examine the case where a pawner attempts to shortcut a sale by attaching a condition to the pawn. The Hanafi school, citing the Prophet's prohibition, declares such a condition invalid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditional clause
The pawner says 'If I do not pay, the pawn becomes your property.' This attaches a future condition to the ownership transfer.
2
Determine the ruling
Imam Muhammad rules that this condition is not permissible (la yajuz). The pawn cannot become a sale without a proper sale contract.
3
Cite the hadith
The Prophet ﷺ said 'Do not suspend the pawn' (لا يعلق الرهن). This hadith directly prohibits such conditional arrangements.
4
Apply the principle
The condition makes the pawn's status uncertain, which is prohibited. The pawn remains a pawn; the condition is void.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ابن رستم عن محمد رحمهما الله تعالى : رجل رهن رجلاً ثوباً فقال له إن لم أعطك كذا وكذا فهو بيع لك بما لك علي قال : لا يجوز وقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام لا يعلق الرهن هو هذا. ولو رهن الغاصب بالمغصوب رهناً والمغصوب قائم في يده وهو مقربه ثم رده على المغصوب منه ثم هلك الرهن عند المرتهن فالمغصوب منه ضامن الأقل من قيمة المغصوب وقيمة الرهن لأن أخذه على جهة الضمان وليس يكون المغصوب ديناً يدفع به رهناً ولكنه لما رهنه صار رهناً وإن لم يكن الأخذ صحيحاً.
Ibn Rustam from Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on them both): A man pawned a garment to a man and said to him: 'If I do not give you such-and-such, then it is a sale to you for what you have against me.' He said: It is not permissible, and his saying, peace and blessings be upon him, 'Do not suspend the pawn' is this. And if a usurper pawns the usurped property as a pawn, and the usurped property remains in his hand and he is holding it, then he returns it to the original owner, then the pawn is destroyed with the mortgagee, then the original owner is liable for the lesser of the value of the usurped property and the value of the pawn, because he took it on the basis of guarantee, and the usurped property does not become a debt that can be defended by a pawn, but when he pawned it, it became a pawn even if the taking was not valid.
Source pages p. 435

Commentary
This passage contains two distinct rulings. The first, transmitted by Ibn Rustam from Imam Muhammad, addresses a common trick: a pawner says to the mortgagee, 'If I do not repay you by such date, then the pawn becomes your property in lieu of the debt.' This is a conditional sale (بيع معلق) disguised as a pawn. Imam Muhammad rules this invalid, citing the hadith 'Do not suspend the pawn' (لا يعلق الرهن), which prohibits such conditional agreements that bypass the proper sale process. The second ruling deals with a usurper (غاصب) who has taken someone's property and then pawns that very property to a third party. If the usurper later returns the usurped property to its original owner, and then the pawn is destroyed with the mortgagee, the original owner becomes liable to the mortgagee for the lesser of the value of the usurped property and the value of the pawn. This is because the original owner received the property from the usurper under the basis of guarantee (ضمان), i.e., the usurper's obligation to return it. The usurped property does not itself become a debt that can be secured by a pawn, but the act of pawning it by the usurper created a valid pawn contract with the mortgagee, even though the original seizure was invalid. Therefore, when the original owner retakes his property, he steps into the shoes of the pawner and becomes responsible for the pawn's loss.

Key Terms
لا يعلق الرهن (la yu'allaqu al-rahn): The hadith forbidding that the pawn be made conditional on a future event that would change its legal status (e.g., becoming a sale upon default).
غاصب (ghasib): Usurper; one who takes someone else's property without legal right.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Rustam's transmission from Imam Muhammad, what is the ruling if a pawner says 'If I do not pay, the pawn becomes your property'?
A) It is permissible and the pawn becomes a sale upon default
B) It is not permissible, and the pawn remains a pawn
C) It is permissible only if the mortgagee agrees
D) It is valid only if witnessed

Key Takeaway
A pawn cannot be made conditional to become a sale; the condition is void.

Usurper's Pawn: Liability of the Original Owner
Ruling on usurper's pawn and owner's liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a usurper pawns usurped property and the pawn is destroyed after return to the owner, and explain the basis of liability.

Core Idea
The original owner is liable for the lesser of the value of the usurped property and the pawn value when the usurper's pawn is destroyed after return.

This lesson deals with a complex scenario: a usurper (ghasib) pawns the very property he has wrongfully taken to a third party. If he later returns the property to its rightful owner, and the pawn is then destroyed with the mortgagee, what is the legal position? The Hanafi school provides a precise rule based on the guarantee inherent in the contract.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and actions
The usurper (A) takes property from owner (B) and pawns it to mortgagee (C). The property is in A's hand at pawning. Later, A returns the property to B. Then the pawn is destroyed while with C.
2
Determine the status of the pawn
The usurper's pawning is valid: the pawn becomes a valid security even though the seizure was invalid. The property does not become a debt of B but is pawned by A.
3
Apply the guarantee principle
When B takes back his property from A, he takes it on the basis of guarantee (daman) – i.e., he steps into A's shoes regarding the pawn contract. Thus B becomes liable to C for the pawn.
4
Calculate the liability
B is liable for the lesser of two values: the value of the usurped property (original) and the value of the pawn (which is the property itself). This is because B's guarantee is limited to the value of what he received (the property) and the value of the pawn (the same property).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ابن رستم عن محمد رحمهما الله تعالى : رجل رهن رجلاً ثوباً فقال له إن لم أعطك كذا وكذا فهو بيع لك بما لك علي قال : لا يجوز وقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام لا يعلق الرهن هو هذا. ولو رهن الغاصب بالمغصوب رهناً والمغصوب قائم في يده وهو مقربه ثم رده على المغصوب منه ثم هلك الرهن عند المرتهن فالمغصوب منه ضامن الأقل من قيمة المغصوب وقيمة الرهن لأن أخذه على جهة الضمان وليس يكون المغصوب ديناً يدفع به رهناً ولكنه لما رهنه صار رهناً وإن لم يكن الأخذ صحيحاً.
Ibn Rustam from Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on them both): A man pawned a garment to a man and said to him: 'If I do not give you such-and-such, then it is a sale to you for what you have against me.' He said: It is not permissible, and his saying, peace and blessings be upon him, 'Do not suspend the pawn' is this. And if a usurper pawns the usurped property as a pawn, and the usurped property remains in his hand and he is holding it, then he returns it to the original owner, then the pawn is destroyed with the mortgagee, then the original owner is liable for the lesser of the value of the usurped property and the value of the pawn, because he took it on the basis of guarantee, and the usurped property does not become a debt that can be defended by a pawn, but when he pawned it, it became a pawn even if the taking was not valid.
Source pages p. 435

Commentary
This passage contains two distinct rulings. The first, transmitted by Ibn Rustam from Imam Muhammad, addresses a common trick: a pawner says to the mortgagee, 'If I do not repay you by such date, then the pawn becomes your property in lieu of the debt.' This is a conditional sale (بيع معلق) disguised as a pawn. Imam Muhammad rules this invalid, citing the hadith 'Do not suspend the pawn' (لا يعلق الرهن), which prohibits such conditional agreements that bypass the proper sale process. The second ruling deals with a usurper (غاصب) who has taken someone's property and then pawns that very property to a third party. If the usurper later returns the usurped property to its original owner, and then the pawn is destroyed with the mortgagee, the original owner becomes liable to the mortgagee for the lesser of the value of the usurped property and the value of the pawn. This is because the original owner received the property from the usurper under the basis of guarantee (ضمان), i.e., the usurper's obligation to return it. The usurped property does not itself become a debt that can be secured by a pawn, but the act of pawning it by the usurper created a valid pawn contract with the mortgagee, even though the original seizure was invalid. Therefore, when the original owner retakes his property, he steps into the shoes of the pawner and becomes responsible for the pawn's loss.

Key Terms
غاصب (ghasib): Usurper; one who takes someone else's property without legal right.
ضمان (daman): Guarantee; the obligation to compensate for loss or damage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling on a usurper's pawn, if the pawn is destroyed after the property is returned to the owner, the owner is liable for:
A) The full value of the usurped property
B) The full value of the pawn
C) The lesser of the value of the usurped property and the value of the pawn
D) Nothing, because he did not pawn it

Key Takeaway
The original owner stepping into the usurper's shoes for the pawn is liable for the lesser of the property value and the pawn value.

Pledgee's Duty to Preserve and Claim of Destruction
Rulings on pledgee's duties and claim of destruction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the pledgee's preservation duty and identify when he must produce the pledge upon the pledgor's claim of destruction.

Core Idea
The pledgee preserves the pledge; only if the pledgor claims destruction must he produce it.

This lesson examines the pledgee's primary duty of preservation and the procedural rule regarding claims of destruction. The Hanafi school balances the rights of both parties: the pledgee holds possession but cannot use the pledge, and the pledgor must still pay if he challenges the pledge's existence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the pledgee's core duties
List the actions the pledgee must and must not do with the pledge (preservation, no use, etc.).
2
Understand the claim of destruction scenario
Focus on when the pledgor claims the pledge is destroyed: the pledgee must produce it or prove its existence because of the possibility it still exists.
3
Contrast with no claim of destruction
If the pledgor does not claim destruction, the pledgee need not produce it because the pledgor acknowledges the debt.
4
Examine the killing of a pledged slave
Note the difference: if a third party kills the slave by mistake, the value is paid by the clan over three years, and the pledgor is not forced to produce evidence.
The substitute (value) replaces the pledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرهن في يد المرتهن لا يمكنه من البيع حتى يقبض الدين فإذا قضى سلم الرهن ولا ينتفع المرتهن بالرهن استخداماً وسكنى ولبساً وإجارة وإعارة ويحفظ بنفسه وزوجته يكلف باستيفاء نجم قد حل إذا ادعى الراهن هلاكه لاحتمال الهلاك بخلاف ما إذا لم يدع الراهن هلاكه لأنه لا فائدة في إحضاره مع إقراره وهذا بخلاف ما إذا قتل رجل خطأ العبد الرهن حتى قضى بالقيمة على عاقلته في ثلاث سنين حيث لا يجبر الراهن وفيما تقدم صار ديناً بفعله ولا بد من إحضار جميع القيمة لأنه يقوم مقام العين لكونها بدلاً عنها. ولو وضع الرهن على يد عدل وأذن بالإيداع ففعل ثم جاء المرتهن فطلب دينه لا يكلف إحضاره لأنه لم يؤتمن عليه حيث وضع على يد غيره فلم يكن تسليمه في قدرته وكذا لو وضعه العدل في يد من في عياله وغاب وطلب المرتهن دينه والذي في يده الرهن يقر بالوديعة من العدل ويقول لا أدري لمن هو يجبر الراهن على قضاء الدين لأن إحضار الرهن ليس على المرتهن لأنه لم يقبض، وكذا إذا غاب العدل ولا يدري أين هو لما قلنا بخلاف ما إذا جحد الذي أودعه العدل الرهن بأن قال هو مالي حيث لا يرجع المرتهن على الراهن بشيء حتى يثبت أنه رهن لأنه لما جحد فقد توى المال والتوى على المرتهن فتحقق الاستيفاء فلا يملك المطالبة به. وفي الفتاوى الغياثية ولو رهن الذمي خمراً عند مسلم كان مضموناً عليه بالدين اهـ. وفي الينابيع : لو تزوج امرأة على دراهم أو دنانير بعينها وأخذ بها رهناً لم يصح عندنا خلافاً لزفر.
The pledge in the hand of the pledgee: he cannot be compelled to sell until he receives the debt. When he pays, he surrenders the pledge. Nor may the pledgee benefit from the pledge by use, residence, clothing, lease, or loan. He preserves it himself and his wife. He is required to collect an installment that has fallen due if the pledgor claims its destruction, because of possibility of destruction, unlike if the pledgor does not claim destruction, because there is no benefit in bringing it forth with his acknowledgment. This is contrary to if a man kills the pledged slave by mistake and the value is adjudged against his clan in three years, where the pledgor is not forced (to produce evidence). In what preceded, it became a debt by his action, and it is necessary to bring the entire value because it stands in place of the property, being its substitute. If he places the pledge in the hand of a trustee and authorizes the deposit, and he does so, then the pledgee comes and demands his debt, he is not required to bring it because he was not entrusted with it, since it was placed with another, so its delivery was not in his power. Similarly, if the trustee places it in the hand of someone under his care and goes away, and the pledgee demands his debt, and the one who has the pledge acknowledges the deposit from the trustee and says, 'I do not know whose it is,' the pledgor is forced to pay the debt because bringing the pledge is not upon the pledgee since he did not take possession. Also, if the trustee is absent and no one knows where he is, for what we said. Unlike if the one whom the trustee deposited the pledge denies it, saying, 'It is my property,' where the pledgee cannot claim anything from the pledgor until he proves it is a pledge, because since he denied, the property is lost and destroyed for the pledgee, so satisfaction is realized, and he has no right to demand it. In Al-Fatawa al-Ghiyathiyya: If a dhimmi pledges wine to a Muslim, it is guaranteed against the debt. In Al-Yanabi': If a man marries a woman on specific dirhams or dinars and takes a pledge for it, it is not valid according to us, contrary to Zufar.
Source pages p. 438

Commentary
This passage is a summary of several rulings from the beginning of the book on pledge. It first repeats the previous rulings: the pledgee cannot be forced to sell, the pledge is returned upon payment, and the pledgee cannot use the pledge. Then it introduces new rulings. The pledgee must preserve the pledge himself or through his wife (as a trusted person). If an installment is due and the pledgor claims the pledge is destroyed, the pledgee is required to produce it (or prove its existence) because of the possibility it still exists; but if the pledgor does not claim destruction, there is no need to produce it since he acknowledges the debt. This is contrasted with the case of a pledged slave being killed by mistake: the value is payable in three years by the killer's clan, and the pledgor is not forced to prove anything. The discussion then shifts to when the pledge is placed with a trustee (عدل). If the pledgee later demands his debt, he cannot be forced to bring the pledge because he no longer possesses it. If the trustee gives it to someone else and disappears, the current holder may not know the owner, so the pledgor must pay the debt. However, if the person holding the pledge denies it is a pledge and claims it as his own, then the pledgee cannot reclaim the debt from the pledgor until he proves it was a pledge, because the property is lost and the pledgee is considered satisfied. Finally, two fatwas are cited: one from Al-Fatawa al-Ghiyathiyya regarding a dhimmi pledging wine to a Muslim (it is guaranteed against the debt, meaning the Muslim must compensate if lost), and one from Al-Yanabi' where a marriage on specific coins with a pledge for the dower is invalid according to the Hanafi school, contrary to Zufar (a Hanafi scholar).

Key Terms
نجم قد حل (najm qad halla): An installment that has become due.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is the pledgee required to produce the pledge?
A) Whenever the debt is due.
B) Only when the pledgor claims the pledge is destroyed.
C) Whenever the pledgee wants to sell.
D) Only when the pledgor has not paid for a year.

Key Takeaway
The pledgee must preserve the pledge and produce it only if the pledgor claims destruction; otherwise, no production is required.

Rulings on the Trustee (عدل) in Pledge Contracts
Rulings on pledge placed with a trustee (عدل).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rulings when a pledge is deposited with a trustee, including scenarios of trustee absence and denial.

Core Idea
When a pledge is with a trustee, the pledgee is not liable for production; the pledgor must pay even if the trustee disappears.

This lesson covers the trustee (عدل) as a neutral holder of the pledge. The Hanafi school clarifies the responsibilities of the parties when the trustee has possession, especially when the trustee absconds or when the person holding the pledge denies it is a pledge.

Guided Path
1
Understand the trustee's role
The trustee holds the pledge on behalf of both parties; the pledgee does not have possession.
2
First scenario: pledgee demands debt
If the pledgee demands his debt, he cannot be forced to bring the pledge because he is not in possession.
3
Second scenario: trustee gives to another and disappears
If the trustee gives the pledge to someone else and disappears, the pledgor must pay the debt because the pledgee cannot produce it.
The current holder acknowledges deposit but does not know owner.
4
Third scenario: the holder denies it is a pledge
If the person holding the pledge claims it is his own property, the pledgee cannot claim from the pledgor until he proves it was a pledge.
Because the property is lost (توى) and the pledgee is satisfied.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرهن في يد المرتهن لا يمكنه من البيع حتى يقبض الدين فإذا قضى سلم الرهن ولا ينتفع المرتهن بالرهن استخداماً وسكنى ولبساً وإجارة وإعارة ويحفظ بنفسه وزوجته يكلف باستيفاء نجم قد حل إذا ادعى الراهن هلاكه لاحتمال الهلاك بخلاف ما إذا لم يدع الراهن هلاكه لأنه لا فائدة في إحضاره مع إقراره وهذا بخلاف ما إذا قتل رجل خطأ العبد الرهن حتى قضى بالقيمة على عاقلته في ثلاث سنين حيث لا يجبر الراهن وفيما تقدم صار ديناً بفعله ولا بد من إحضار جميع القيمة لأنه يقوم مقام العين لكونها بدلاً عنها. ولو وضع الرهن على يد عدل وأذن بالإيداع ففعل ثم جاء المرتهن فطلب دينه لا يكلف إحضاره لأنه لم يؤتمن عليه حيث وضع على يد غيره فلم يكن تسليمه في قدرته وكذا لو وضعه العدل في يد من في عياله وغاب وطلب المرتهن دينه والذي في يده الرهن يقر بالوديعة من العدل ويقول لا أدري لمن هو يجبر الراهن على قضاء الدين لأن إحضار الرهن ليس على المرتهن لأنه لم يقبض، وكذا إذا غاب العدل ولا يدري أين هو لما قلنا بخلاف ما إذا جحد الذي أودعه العدل الرهن بأن قال هو مالي حيث لا يرجع المرتهن على الراهن بشيء حتى يثبت أنه رهن لأنه لما جحد فقد توى المال والتوى على المرتهن فتحقق الاستيفاء فلا يملك المطالبة به. وفي الفتاوى الغياثية ولو رهن الذمي خمراً عند مسلم كان مضموناً عليه بالدين اهـ. وفي الينابيع : لو تزوج امرأة على دراهم أو دنانير بعينها وأخذ بها رهناً لم يصح عندنا خلافاً لزفر.
The pledge in the hand of the pledgee: he cannot be compelled to sell until he receives the debt. When he pays, he surrenders the pledge. Nor may the pledgee benefit from the pledge by use, residence, clothing, lease, or loan. He preserves it himself and his wife. He is required to collect an installment that has fallen due if the pledgor claims its destruction, because of possibility of destruction, unlike if the pledgor does not claim destruction, because there is no benefit in bringing it forth with his acknowledgment. This is contrary to if a man kills the pledged slave by mistake and the value is adjudged against his clan in three years, where the pledgor is not forced (to produce evidence). In what preceded, it became a debt by his action, and it is necessary to bring the entire value because it stands in place of the property, being its substitute. If he places the pledge in the hand of a trustee and authorizes the deposit, and he does so, then the pledgee comes and demands his debt, he is not required to bring it because he was not entrusted with it, since it was placed with another, so its delivery was not in his power. Similarly, if the trustee places it in the hand of someone under his care and goes away, and the pledgee demands his debt, and the one who has the pledge acknowledges the deposit from the trustee and says, 'I do not know whose it is,' the pledgor is forced to pay the debt because bringing the pledge is not upon the pledgee since he did not take possession. Also, if the trustee is absent and no one knows where he is, for what we said. Unlike if the one whom the trustee deposited the pledge denies it, saying, 'It is my property,' where the pledgee cannot claim anything from the pledgor until he proves it is a pledge, because since he denied, the property is lost and destroyed for the pledgee, so satisfaction is realized, and he has no right to demand it. In Al-Fatawa al-Ghiyathiyya: If a dhimmi pledges wine to a Muslim, it is guaranteed against the debt. In Al-Yanabi': If a man marries a woman on specific dirhams or dinars and takes a pledge for it, it is not valid according to us, contrary to Zufar.
Source pages p. 438

Commentary
This passage is a summary of several rulings from the beginning of the book on pledge. It first repeats the previous rulings: the pledgee cannot be forced to sell, the pledge is returned upon payment, and the pledgee cannot use the pledge. Then it introduces new rulings. The pledgee must preserve the pledge himself or through his wife (as a trusted person). If an installment is due and the pledgor claims the pledge is destroyed, the pledgee is required to produce it (or prove its existence) because of the possibility it still exists; but if the pledgor does not claim destruction, there is no need to produce it since he acknowledges the debt. This is contrasted with the case of a pledged slave being killed by mistake: the value is payable in three years by the killer's clan, and the pledgor is not forced to prove anything. The discussion then shifts to when the pledge is placed with a trustee (عدل). If the pledgee later demands his debt, he cannot be forced to bring the pledge because he no longer possesses it. If the trustee gives it to someone else and disappears, the current holder may not know the owner, so the pledgor must pay the debt. However, if the person holding the pledge denies it is a pledge and claims it as his own, then the pledgee cannot reclaim the debt from the pledgor until he proves it was a pledge, because the property is lost and the pledgee is considered satisfied. Finally, two fatwas are cited: one from Al-Fatawa al-Ghiyathiyya regarding a dhimmi pledging wine to a Muslim (it is guaranteed against the debt, meaning the Muslim must compensate if lost), and one from Al-Yanabi' where a marriage on specific coins with a pledge for the dower is invalid according to the Hanafi school, contrary to Zufar (a Hanafi scholar).

Key Terms
يد عدل (yad 'adl): A neutral trustee holding the pledge on behalf of both parties.
توى المال (tawa al-mal): The property is lost or destroyed without trace.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a trustee deposits the pledged item with a third party and disappears, and the third party acknowledges the deposit but does not know the owner, what is the ruling?
A) The pledgee must sue the third party.
B) The pledgor must pay the debt.
C) The debt is canceled.
D) The trustee's family must pay.

Key Takeaway
When a pledge is with a trustee, the pledgor bears the risk of the trustee's absence; the pledgee is not required to produce the pledge.

Special Fatwas: Wine Pledge and Marriage Pledge
Fatwas on special pledge cases: wine and marriage.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on a dhimmi pledging wine to a Muslim and on taking a pledge for the dower in a marriage contract, including the disagreement with Zufar.

Core Idea
Wine pledged by a dhimmi is guaranteed against the debt; a pledge for specific dower items in marriage is invalid.

This lesson covers two special fatwas from later Hanafi works. First, wine, which is not valuable property for Muslims, is still valid as a pledge from a dhimmi, and the Muslim pledgee must guarantee its value. Second, if a marriage dower is specified as particular coins and a pledge is taken for those coins, the pledge is invalid according to the majority Hanafis, but Zufar disagreed.

Guided Path
1
First fatwa: wine pledged by a dhimmi
A dhimmi pledges wine to a Muslim. The Muslim must guarantee its value against the debt.
Wine is not property for Muslims but is property for dhimmis.
2
Second fatwa: marriage on specific coins with a pledge
A man marries a woman on specific dirhams or dinars and takes a pledge for that dower. The pledge is invalid according to the Hanafi school.
The dower must be determined in the contract; the pledge is separate.
3
Note the ikhtilaf with Zufar
Zufar allows this practice; the majority Hanafis do not.
Zufar is a Hanafi scholar known for independent opinions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرهن في يد المرتهن لا يمكنه من البيع حتى يقبض الدين فإذا قضى سلم الرهن ولا ينتفع المرتهن بالرهن استخداماً وسكنى ولبساً وإجارة وإعارة ويحفظ بنفسه وزوجته يكلف باستيفاء نجم قد حل إذا ادعى الراهن هلاكه لاحتمال الهلاك بخلاف ما إذا لم يدع الراهن هلاكه لأنه لا فائدة في إحضاره مع إقراره وهذا بخلاف ما إذا قتل رجل خطأ العبد الرهن حتى قضى بالقيمة على عاقلته في ثلاث سنين حيث لا يجبر الراهن وفيما تقدم صار ديناً بفعله ولا بد من إحضار جميع القيمة لأنه يقوم مقام العين لكونها بدلاً عنها. ولو وضع الرهن على يد عدل وأذن بالإيداع ففعل ثم جاء المرتهن فطلب دينه لا يكلف إحضاره لأنه لم يؤتمن عليه حيث وضع على يد غيره فلم يكن تسليمه في قدرته وكذا لو وضعه العدل في يد من في عياله وغاب وطلب المرتهن دينه والذي في يده الرهن يقر بالوديعة من العدل ويقول لا أدري لمن هو يجبر الراهن على قضاء الدين لأن إحضار الرهن ليس على المرتهن لأنه لم يقبض، وكذا إذا غاب العدل ولا يدري أين هو لما قلنا بخلاف ما إذا جحد الذي أودعه العدل الرهن بأن قال هو مالي حيث لا يرجع المرتهن على الراهن بشيء حتى يثبت أنه رهن لأنه لما جحد فقد توى المال والتوى على المرتهن فتحقق الاستيفاء فلا يملك المطالبة به. وفي الفتاوى الغياثية ولو رهن الذمي خمراً عند مسلم كان مضموناً عليه بالدين اهـ. وفي الينابيع : لو تزوج امرأة على دراهم أو دنانير بعينها وأخذ بها رهناً لم يصح عندنا خلافاً لزفر.
The pledge in the hand of the pledgee: he cannot be compelled to sell until he receives the debt. When he pays, he surrenders the pledge. Nor may the pledgee benefit from the pledge by use, residence, clothing, lease, or loan. He preserves it himself and his wife. He is required to collect an installment that has fallen due if the pledgor claims its destruction, because of possibility of destruction, unlike if the pledgor does not claim destruction, because there is no benefit in bringing it forth with his acknowledgment. This is contrary to if a man kills the pledged slave by mistake and the value is adjudged against his clan in three years, where the pledgor is not forced (to produce evidence). Pledgee Cannot Be Forced to Sell the Pledge
Commentary on the ruling that the pledgee cannot be forced to sell the pledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a pledgee cannot be forced to sell the pledge and explain the qiyas to sale retention.

Core Idea
The pledgee retains the pledge as security until full payment—no forced sale.

In this passage, the commentator clarifies the nature of rahn (pledge) as perpetual custody. The pledgor may wish to sell the pledge to repay the debt, but the pledgee cannot be compelled to allow the sale. This ruling is based on the analogy of retention in sale (حبس المبيع).

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its subject
The commentator states that if the pledge is in the pledgee's hand, he cannot be forced to sell until he receives the debt. This establishes the pledgee's right of retention.
The ruling applies when the pledgee holds possession.
2
Understand the ratio legis (علة) — perpetual custody
The nature of rahn is perpetual custody (حبس دائم) until the debt is paid, not payment from the sale. This is the underlying rationale.
This distinguishes rahn from a mere means of enforcement.
3
Explore the partial payment scenario
If the pledgor pays only part of the debt, the pledgee may hold the entire pledge until the remainder is collected. The commentator analogizes to the seller's retention in sale.
Partial payment does not trigger proportional release.
4
Apply the qiyas to sale retention
The pledgee's right is similar to the seller's right to retain the sold item until full payment (حبس المبيع). In both cases, the holder is entitled to full satisfaction before release.
The dalil is qiyas jaliy (clear analogy).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (فإن كان الرهن في يد المرتهن لا يمكنه من البيع حتى يقبض الدين) أي لو أراد الراهن أن يبيع الرهن لكي يقضي بثمنه الدين لا يجبر المرتهن أن يمكنه من البيع حتى يقبض الدين لأن حكم الرهن الحبس الدائم إلى أن يقضي الدين لا القضاء من ثمنه على ما بينا من قبل، فلو قضاه البعض فله أن يحبس كل الرهن حتى يستوفي البقية كما في حبس المبيع. قال رحمه الله : (فإذا قضى سلم الرهن أي إذا قضى الراهن جميع الدين سلم المرتهن الرهن إليه الزوال المانع من التسليم لوصول حق المرتهن إليه ، فلو هلك الرهن بعد قضاء الدين قبل تسليمه إلى الراهن استرد الراهن ما قضاه من الدين لأنه تبين بالهلاك أنه صار مستوفياً من وقت القبض السابق فكان الثاني استيفاء بعد استيفاء فيجب رده . وهذا لأنه بإيفاء الدين لا ينفسخ الرهن حتى يرده إلى صاحبه فيكون مضموناً على حاله بعد قضاء الدين ما لم يسلمه إلى الراهن أو يبرئه المرتهن عن الدين، وكذا لو فسخا الرهن لا ينفسخ ما دام في يده حتى كان للمرتهن أن بعد الفسخ حتى يستوفي دينه . ولو هلك بعد الفسخ يكون كما لو هلك قبله فيكون هالكاً بدينه بخلاف ما إذا هلك بعد الإبراء حيث لا يضمن استحساناً لأنه لم يبق رهناً لأن بقاءه رهناً بأمرين بالقبض والدين، فإذا مات أحدهما لم يبق رهناً وقد قدمناه مفصلاً.
He (the commentator) said, may Allah have mercy on him: (If the pledge is in the hand of the pledgee, he cannot be compelled to sell until he receives the debt.) Meaning: if the pledgor wants to sell the pledge to pay off the debt with its price, the pledgee is not forced to enable the sale until he receives the debt, because the ruling of pledge is perpetual custody until the debt is paid, not payment from its price as we explained before. So if he pays part of it, he may hold all of the pledge until he collects the remainder, just as in the withholding of the sold item. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (When he pays, he surrenders the pledge.) Meaning: when the pledgor pays the entire debt, the pledgee surrenders the pledge to him, removing the impediment to delivery due to the arrival of the pledgee's right. So if the pledge perishes after payment of the debt before being delivered to the pledgor, the pledgor recovers what he paid of the debt, because it becomes clear through its perishing that he (the pledgee) had already received satisfaction from the prior possession, so the second is satisfaction after satisfaction, so it must be returned. This is because by paying the debt, the pledge is not dissolved until he returns it to its owner, so it remains in his liability as before after payment of the debt unless he delivers it to the pledgor or the pledgee exonerates him from the debt. Similarly, if they rescind the pledge, it is not dissolved as long as it is in his hand, to the extent that the pledgee may after rescission still collect his debt. And if it perishes after rescission, it is as if it perished before, so it perishes against the debt, unlike if it perishes after exoneration, where he does not guarantee, by istihsan, because it no longer remains a pledge, because its continuance as a pledge depends on two things: possession and debt. When one of them ceases, it is no longer a pledge. We have already elaborated this.
Source pages p. 438

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) from Al-Bahr al-Raiq explaining two consecutive rulings from the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq. The first ruling states that if a pledge is in the hands of the pledgee (مرتهن), the pledgor (راهن) cannot force the pledgee to sell the pledge to repay the debt. The commentator clarifies that the nature of rahn (pledge) is perpetual custody (حبس دائم) until the debt is paid; it is not a means of selling to settle the debt. Therefore, the pledgee has the right to retain the entire pledge even after partial payment, until the full debt is collected. This is analogous to the right of retention in a sale (حبس المبيع). The second ruling states that when the pledgor pays the entire debt, the pledgee must surrender the pledge. However, the pledge contract does not dissolve automatically upon payment; it remains in effect until actual delivery or exoneration. If the pledge perishes after payment but before delivery, the pledgee is deemed to have already received his debt from the time of the original possession (since the pledge was in his hand as security), so the debt payment is considered redundant and must be returned to the pledgor. The commentator further explains that if both parties rescind the pledge (فسخ), it still does not dissolve as long as the pledgee holds it, and the pledgee retains the right to collect his debt even after rescission. If the pledge perishes after rescission, it is treated as if it perished before rescission, meaning it is considered lost against the debt. However, if the pledgee exonerates (إبراء) the pledgor from the debt, then the pledge ceases to be a pledge because both possession and debt are gone, and if it perishes thereafter, the pledgee is not liable.

Key Terms
الرهن (ar-rahn): A contract in which property is given as security for a debt, with the pledgee holding possession until repayment.
المرتهن (al-murtahin): The creditor who receives the pledge as security.
الراهن (ar-rahin): The debtor who gives the pledge.
الحبس الدائم (al-habs ad-da'im): Permanent custody; the pledgee's right to hold the pledge until the debt is paid.
حبس المبيع (habs al-mabi'): The seller's right to retain the sold item until full payment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, the pledgee's right to retain the pledge is analogous to which scenario?
A) Seller's right to retain sold item until payment.
B) Landlord's right to retain property for unpaid rent.
C) Buyer's right to inspect goods.
D) None of the above.

Key Takeaway
The pledgee's right to retain the pledge until full payment is absolute and cannot be overridden by the pledgor's desire to sell.

Return of Pledge Upon Full Payment and Consequences of Perishing
Commentary on the return of the pledge upon full payment and consequences of perishing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the ruling that the pledgee must return the pledge upon full payment, and identify the consequences if the pledge perishes after payment but before delivery.

Core Idea
Paying the debt does not automatically dissolve the pledge; the pledgee remains liable until delivery.

This passage explains that after full payment, the pledge must be surrendered. However, the pledge contract does not dissolve immediately. If the pledge perishes after payment but before delivery, the pledgee is deemed to have already satisfied the debt from the original possession, so the payment is refunded. The commentator distinguishes between rescission and exoneration.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on return of the pledge
The commentator states that when the pledgor pays the entire debt, the pledgee surrenders the pledge. This is a wajib obligation.
The removal of the debt eliminates the reason for holding.
2
Understand the effect of perishing after payment
If the pledge perishes after payment but before delivery, the pledgee is considered to have already received satisfaction from the original possession. Therefore, the payment becomes redundant and must be returned to the pledgor.
The pledge remains in effect until delivery.
3
Distinguish between rescission and exoneration
If the parties rescind the pledge, it does not dissolve as long as it is in the pledgee's hand; the pledgee may still collect his debt. But if the pledgee exonerates (ibra') the pledgor, the pledge ceases to exist, and perishing thereafter has no liability.
Exoneration removes the debt, rescission does not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (فإن كان الرهن في يد المرتهن لا يمكنه من البيع حتى يقبض الدين) أي لو أراد الراهن أن يبيع الرهن لكي يقضي بثمنه الدين لا يجبر المرتهن أن يمكنه من البيع حتى يقبض الدين لأن حكم الرهن الحبس الدائم إلى أن يقضي الدين لا القضاء من ثمنه على ما بينا من قبل، فلو قضاه البعض فله أن يحبس كل الرهن حتى يستوفي البقية كما في حبس المبيع. قال رحمه الله : (فإذا قضى سلم الرهن أي إذا قضى الراهن جميع الدين سلم المرتهن الرهن إليه الزوال المانع من التسليم لوصول حق المرتهن إليه ، فلو هلك الرهن بعد قضاء الدين قبل تسليمه إلى الراهن استرد الراهن ما قضاه من الدين لأنه تبين بالهلاك أنه صار مستوفياً من وقت القبض السابق فكان الثاني استيفاء بعد استيفاء فيجب رده . وهذا لأنه بإيفاء الدين لا ينفسخ الرهن حتى يرده إلى صاحبه فيكون مضموناً على حاله بعد قضاء الدين ما لم يسلمه إلى الراهن أو يبرئه المرتهن عن الدين، وكذا لو فسخا الرهن لا ينفسخ ما دام في يده حتى كان للمرتهن أن بعد الفسخ حتى يستوفي دينه . ولو هلك بعد الفسخ يكون كما لو هلك قبله فيكون هالكاً بدينه بخلاف ما إذا هلك بعد الإبراء حيث لا يضمن استحساناً لأنه لم يبق رهناً لأن بقاءه رهناً بأمرين بالقبض والدين، فإذا مات أحدهما لم يبق رهناً وقد قدمناه مفصلاً.

الرهن (ar-rahn): A contract in which property is given as security for a debt, with the pledgee holding possession until repayment.
المرتهن (al-murtahin): The creditor who receives the pledge as security.
الراهن (ar-rahin): The debtor who gives the pledge.
الإبراء (al-ibra'): Exoneration; the pledgee's discharge of the debt, which dissolves the pledge.
الفسخ (al-faskh): Rescission; the act of annulling the contract by mutual agreement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens to the pledge if the parties rescind the contract but the pledge remains in the pledgee's hand?
A) The pledge is dissolved.
B) The pledgee may still collect his debt.
C) The pledge must be returned immediately.
D) The pledge is no longer a security.

Key Takeaway
Full payment alone does not dissolve the pledge; actual delivery or exoneration is required, and perishing after payment leads to a refund.

Pledgee's Use of the Pledge Without Permission: Ruling and Liability
Commentary on the prohibition of pledgee use without permission.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the pledgee's use of the pledge without permission and identify the legal consequences for various scenarios.

Core Idea
The pledgee’s right is only custody; any use without permission is a transgression that triggers liability but does not void the pledge.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq explains the fundamental principle that the pledgee (مرتهن) has no right to benefit from the pledged item beyond custody. The commentator elaborates on the prohibition of various uses—service, residence, clothing, lease, or loan—and details the legal consequences when the pledgee uses the item with or without the pledgor's permission. The lesson will guide you through the ruling, its proof, and practical applications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage discusses the pledgee using the pledged item. The ruling is that it is haram without the pledgor's permission. Determine the act: using the pledge for benefit (e.g., service, residence, etc.).
The matn explicitly states the prohibition.
2
Understand the reasoning (talil)
The commentator explains that the essence of pledge (رهن) is custody (حبس) until debt repayment, not benefit. Any use beyond custody is transgression (تعدي).
The purpose of rahn is security, not profit for the pledgee.
3
Analyze the scenarios of permission and liability
The passage presents multiple scenarios: use with permission (treated as loan, no liability unless violation), use without permission (guarantor of usurpation), leasing without permission (invalid but may be ratified), and lending to the pledgor (pledge remains intact).
Focus on the shift in liability depending on authorization.
4
Distinguish the Hanafi position from other schools
The Hanafi school strictly prohibits any use without explicit permission. Other schools may allow limited use (e.g., riding a pledged animal with feeding costs).
This ikhtilaf is based on different interpretations of the purpose of rahn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (ولا ينتفع المرتهن بالرهن استخداماً وسكنى ولبساً وإجارة وإعارة) لأن الرهن يقتضي الحبس إلى أن يستوفي دينه دون الانتفاع فلا يجوز الانتفاع إلا بتسليط منه، وإن فعل كان متعدياً ولا يبطل الرهن بالتعدي. قال في المبسوط : وليس للمرتهن أن ينتفع بالمرهون إلا بإذن الراهن فإذا أذن له جاز أن يفعل ما إذن له فيه ولو فعل من غير إذن صار ضامناً بحكم الرهن بحكم وقابضاً الغصب. وإن ترك الاستعمال عاد لكونه رهناً، ولو استعمل الرهن بإذن المرتهن فإن هلك حالة الانتفاع لم يسقط من الدين شيء لأنه بالإذن صار مقبوضاً بحكم العارية، وإن خالف وهلك في حال الاستعمال يضمن ضمان الغصب. وفي المنتقى : لو أودع المرتهن المرهون بإذنه وهلك في يد المودع لم يسقط الدين كما لو أعاره من غيره بإذن الراهن فقد خرج من ضمان المرتهن وله أن يسترده لأن الرهن عقد قائم ولكن مرتفع في زمان الإيداع لما بينا ولو أجره من أجنبي سنة بغير إذن الراهن وانقضت السنة ثم أجاز الراهن الإجارة لم تصح لأن الإجارة لاقت عقداً منتفياً مفسوخاً وللمرتهن أن يأخذها حتى يصير رهناً كما كان، وإن أجاز بعد مضي ستة أشهر جاز ونصف الأجر للمرتهن يتصدق به ونصفها للراهن، وليس للمرتهن أن يعيدها في الرهن كما بينا. وذكر أبو الليث في العيون ولو أعار المرتهن من الراهن ثم مات الراهن فإنه يرجع المرتهن ولا يكون أسوة الغرماء لأن الرهن لم ينفسخ بالإعارة فيكون الرهن في يد المستعير لكونه في يد المعير فكان مقبوضاً له، وبالموت انفسخت الإعارة فعادت يد المرتهن كما كانت . ولو ارتهن جارية ثم أعارها الراهن فولدت عند الراهن ثم ماتت فللمرتهن أو يعيد الولد بحصته لأن الرهن لم ينتقض بإعارة الرهن من الراهن فيسري إلى الولد والله تعالى أعلم. وفي المنتقى : وإذا كان الرهن ثوباً فأذن له الراهن في لبسه يوماً ثم جاء به متخرقاً فقال المرتهن تخرق من لبسه من ذلك اليوم فقال الراهن لم يتخرق من لبسك ولم تلبسه فالقول قول الراهن لأن المرتهن ادعى البراءة عن الضمان لاستعمال الثوب بإذن الراهن وهو ينكر فيكون القول له، فإذا أقر الراهن أنه لبسه في ذلك اليوم وتخرق قبل لبسه أو بعده فالقول قول المرتهن أنه تخرق من لبسه والبينة بينة الراهن لأن الظاهر شاهد للمرتهن لأن فعله وهو اللبس سبب التخرق ظاهراً وغير موهوم فيه في حال التخرق في السبب الظاهر دون الموهوم والله تعالى أعلم.
He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (Nor may the pledgee benefit from the pledge by using it as a servant, residence, clothing, lease, or loan.) Because the pledge necessitates custody until he receives his debt, not benefit. So it is not permissible to benefit except with his (the pledgor's) authorization. If he does so, he is transgressing, and the pledge is not invalidated by transgression. Al-Mabsut says: The pledgee may not benefit from the pledged item except with the pledgor's permission. If he permits him, he may do what he permitted. If he does so without permission, he becomes a guarantor according to the law of pledge and a possessor by usurpation. If he abandons use, it returns to being a pledge. If the pledgee uses it with the pledgee's permission (text says 'بإذن المرتهن' but context suggests 'بإذن الراهن' - see note), then if it perishes during use, nothing of the debt is dropped, because by permission it becomes possessed as a loan. If he violates and it perishes during use, he guarantees as a guarantor of usurpation. In Al-Muntaqa: If the pledgee deposits the pledged item with his permission and it perishes in the hand of the depositary, the debt is not dropped, just as if he lent it to another with the pledgor's permission. It has left the pledgee's liability and he may retrieve it because the pledge is a subsisting contract but suspended during the deposit time as we explained. If he leases it to a third party for a year without the pledgor's permission, and the year passes, then the pledgor validates the lease, it is not valid because the lease encountered a contract that was non-existent and dissolved. The pledgee may take it so that it becomes a pledge as before. If he validates after six months have passed, it is valid, and half the rent is for the pledgee to give in charity and half for the pledgor. The pledgee may not return it to the pledge as we explained. Abu al-Layth mentioned in Al-Uyun: If the pledgee lends it to the pledgor, then the pledgor dies, the pledgee takes recourse and is not equal to other creditors because the pledge was not dissolved by the loan; it was in the hand of the borrower (pledgor) because it was in the hand of the lender (pledgee), so it was in his possession. Upon death, the loan dissolves and the pledgee's hand returns as before. If he takes a female slave as pledge, then the pledgor lends her and she gives birth while with the pledgor, then dies, the pledgee has the offspring [as part of the pledge] or returns it with its share [of the debt?] because the pledge was not nullified by lending the pledge from the pledgor, so it extends to the offspring. And Allah knows best. In Al-Muntaqa: If the pledge is a garment, and the pledgor permits him to wear it for a day, then he brings it torn, and the pledgee says it tore from his wearing that day, and the pledgor says it did not tear from your wearing and you did not wear it. The word is the pledgor's word because the pledgee claimed discharge from liability due to using the garment with the pledgor's permission, and he denies it, so the word is his. If the pledgor admits that he wore it that day and that it tore before or after wearing, then the word is the pledgee's that it tore from his wearing. The evidence is the pledgor's evidence because the apparent circumstance is a witness for the pledgee, because his action (wearing) is the apparent cause of tearing, not speculative. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 439

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn ruling that the pledgee may not benefit from the pledge through use (as a servant), residence, clothing, lease, or loan. The commentator explains that the purpose of rahn is purely custodial (حبس), not beneficial use. Any use without the pledgor's explicit permission constitutes transgression (تعدي), but does not invalidate the pledge contract itself. If the pledgee uses it with permission, it becomes a loan (عارية) and the pledgee is not liable for loss during use unless he violates conditions. If he uses without permission, he becomes a guarantor for the value (ضمان الغصب) and is liable if it perishes. The commentary then details various scenarios: depositing the pledge with a third party, leasing it without permission, the pledgee lending it to the pledgor, and the case of a torn garment. In each, the key principle is that the pledgee's rights are limited to custody, and any use or disposition without authorization shifts liability. The author also discusses the validity of ratification (إجازة) after the fact, and the distribution of rent when a lease is ratified partially. The passage emphasizes the Hanafi position that the pledgee cannot exploit the pledge for personal gain, distinguishing it from some other schools.

Key Terms
استخداماً (istikhdaman): Using the pledged item (e.g., slave) as a servant.
سكنى (sukna): Using the pledged property as a residence.
إجارة (ijarah): Leasing out the pledged item to others.
إعارة (i'arah): Lending the pledged item to someone else.
ضمان الغصب (daman al-ghasb): Liability equivalent to that of a usurper, i.e., guaranteeing the value if the item perishes while in unauthorized use.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the pledgee uses the pledged item with the pledgor's permission, and it perishes during use, what is the effect on the debt?
A) The debt is reduced by the value of the item.
B) The debt remains fully due, and the pledgee is not liable.
C) The debt is canceled because the pledge is lost.
D) The pledgee must pay the value of the item to the pledgor.

Key Takeaway
The pledgee's right is limited to custody; any use without permission is a transgression that triggers liability but does not invalidate the pledge contract.
